I think we just gotta look at it on a case by case basis. Stealing percentage of wage is wrong but its legal because the government does it all the time. Stealing in the case of piracy in a reletive ethical and legal sense is also wrong, but you could end up breaking laws relating to it without even knowing or any calculated malice being intended since watching that one donated movie on highschool projector still counts as such on a technical level but just isnt enforced. Going further into piracy, you can do it while being ethically in the right for making efforts to preserve media for future generations and study, but only legally in the wrong; see examples of archiving old minecraft versions running through 3rd party launchers, and Library free & donated movie checkout. It would also be hard to make the argument of theft if a media is obtained through digital means since the inherent property of digital media is that its always going to be in a state of infinite replicability. Any tine something is uploaded or downloaded it is cloned 1:1. So how many sales are you actually stealing if you purchase 1 game key, and install it on multiple systems for a LAN party? Or buy 1 key multiple times and then get a DRMless crack of it later to play solely offline during roadtrips?  And in response to something Geneva suggested, is stealing really that wrong if its a dead enemy's gear? They are dead. Im not sure they would get much use out of it or even miss it for that matter.

We have lost sight of what we were agreeing on long ago. Agreeing with Josh has become the new standard, devoid of any memory or understanding of what we were actually agreeing upon. Agreeing with Josh gives us comfort, social cohesion, stability, and purpose. Agreeing with Josh is the glue that binds us. Agreeing with Josh is the hill I'll die on, and I know my peers would die on that hill too, if they had to. I even know some peers who would die on that hill for me, so I don't have to, and I would die on that hill too, to save one of my peers. It's a beautiful thing to be surrounded by people who agree with Josh. It makes me feel like I'm part of something bigger and better than my own meaningless self. Sometimes my dad will come home a little too drunk after work. He'll start beating my mum while I hide under my bed covers not making a sound. Sometimes I wake up in the morning and I think about all the pressures and stresses of school. I realise I don't want to get out of bed. I just want to hide. Every day I head to the breakfast table 10 minutes before the school bus arrives, and my abusive dad is waiting there for me. I can't bare to look him in the eye.   Sometimes it looks like every step I take in life is difficult, draining and terrifying. They say there are so many paths I can choose to walk in this life, but I feel like every path in front of me is painful. I start feeling sorry for myself. I feel like I have become a victim of this hostile and heartless middle schooler environment. My friends and family did this to me. My weird neighbour who stares at me through a window when I walk back from school, he did this to me. The world has fucked me, and I feel all alone. I suffer alone, and nobody seems to notice. How can I suffer like this, but nobody even bats an eye? I think I must be going mad. I wonder if it might simply be less of burden to end this suffering. Maybe people will finally see my suffering when I'm dead. Maybe they'll shed a tear for me, and I'll finally be validated. I'll finally find peace.   In these dark times, I think of Josh. Specifically I am reminded of how I agree with him. I am reminded of all the people around me who agree with Josh too. I realise I respect those people. I value them, and I understand and empathise with their suffering. Then I realise, not only do I respect them, but they respect me. They understand me. They see what's inside me and they resonate with that. They see value in me. They have hope for me, and I have hope for all of them. Sometimes I think about all the people out there who don't agree with Josh, and I think how miserable their lives must be. I realise just how fortunate I am to have found Josh in my life, and to have found this community of people who value me for agreeing with him. It's a weird thing this. I feel like... well... Of course I agree with Josh and always will. Don't think that by saying this I am trying to take away from the fact that I agree with Josh. But it almost feels like, sitting here today, in this moment, contemplating life, I feel that... well... I think that not only do I agree with Josh, but after all this time, I think Josh agrees with me too.

Human, as social beings, has been interacting with each other since ancient times. This kind of interaction can be called as symbiosis, as humans count as biological beings [1]. From these interactions, there's one called theft. The act of thievery is when a human takes away the belonging or service of other human without the other's permission [2].  In conclusion, the act of theft can be said as a parasitic relationship as it deprives other human of their belongings.  Bibliography 1. "symbiosis." Dorland's Illustrated Medical Dictionary. You forgot the 10 awkward seconds before josh raised his hand
While it is easy to assume that stealing is wrong because it causes harm to the victim of the theft, nothing in life is ever as black and white as that. It‚Äôs pretty clear that if you are only stealing for frivolous reasons, and for your own pleasure, then yes; harming someone purely for your own enjoyment is immoral. But consider a poor man whose family is starving, and he has no way of obtaining money. Would it be wrong for him to steal some food to feed his family, if the alternative is them starving? By not stealing, he is allowing multiple people to die, which is a much worse outcome than someone else not making a bit of money for some product. In today‚Äôs society, most theft would be committed against large corporations, since they own most of the capital. But those corporations only have the capital that they do because they exploit land, people, and natural resources in developing nations, so by supporting them by purchasing their goods and services, you are contributing to the harm caused by the immoral practices of those companies. You could even make the argument that stealing in that case is moral, since it harms the people who cause even more harm than you ever could. Another case is when someone is selling something that they have no right to be selling, since the product should be a human right to own instead of a commodity. If a company declared that they owned the air and started charging people to breathe, it would definitely not be wrong to breathe without paying them, since the air does not belong to anyone. As I have pointed out, stealing something that someone else rightfully owns, without any valid reason to steal, is wrong, but the notion that any theft ever is wrong does not hold up because of moral complexity and the capitalist society we live in. The people who hold all the power are the ones who decide what exactly theft is, while being thieves themselves, and we shouldn‚Äôt just mindlessly accept what they say. I‚Äôll pass the mic around now if anyone else wants to add or reply to that.

We were split into groups and forced to defend one of four viewpoints no borders, low regulation immigration, limited immigration, and my group no immigration. Now I won't go into my personal oppinion on immigration, but we had two Liberals in class (they got low regulation immigration). Now the rest of the groups put little to no effort into their arguments besides me and maybe a tiny but if effort on low regulation. Now we were the last group to present and so far low regulation was winning. Ngl it was unbelievably easy to sway the judges in my favor. Unlike my peers I put effort and made solid points that a Middle Schooler couldn't debate with ease, and as I continued on my argument I could see a bunch of my classmates nodding and the two Liberals and my teacher looking like they were going to lose their shit. Me and my group won all four of the judge's votes. Moral of the story, teens are extremely easy to persuade to your side of you make them afraid of the other sides or promise free shit.
